10/02/2022, 11:04 - mehak kataria: Subject:Request for hybrid mode of education for 3rd year outstation students

*Body:*
Respected Sir,

I am (y/n), a third year student from (course name) at (college name). I am an outstation student from (your hometown). I am writing to you about the latest update regarding the re-opening of the university in an offline mode. I understand that this is the decision taken by the University of Delhi.However, I have few concerns about this decision and would request the college to view this decision particularly from the standpoint of third year, outstation students.

My concerns are as follows:
1. DU and colleges do not provide hostel facilities to all outstation students. Which means most of us stay in PG accommodations. Most of the PGs were shut down due to COVID and are not operational. I reached out to my previous PG and they are closed. They will be able to start providing these services only after 1 month as they have to set up the infrastructure all over again. I am sure other PGs will have the same situation.

2. Outstation students will have to look for PG accommodation, which may not be available once they reach Delhi and will have no place to live at.

 3. Financial distress:  PG costs will increase due to COVID protocols and the sudden reopening leading to additional financial burden on parents. Many families,  have been financially burdened since the onset of the pandemic. So for me to come to Delhi for only a couple of months, demands a lot of additional financing

4. Most third year students, including me, have taken up internships during this period which are crucial to our CVs. Due to colleges being offline for so long, we have had to step up and gain exposure ourselves. Offline classes for third years may hence hamper this and lead to students losing their chance at gaining work experience.

6. The mid semester break for 6th semester starts on 13th March and colleges reopen on 20th March. Exam preparation starts from 28th April. This basically means outstation students will end up coming to Delhi just for 9 weeks of education. This seems unnecessary and a waste of time, effort and money. If exams have to be conducted offline then students can plan accordingly as they will know upfront and will make plans accordingly.

7. Maintaining COVID protocols with full capacity is impossible. With 50+ students in a classroom someone is very likely to catch COVID and spread it to other students and faculty.

8. In case an outstation student becomes COVID infected, they will have no place to quarantine and no one to care for them. If they continue to stay at their respective PG's then the entire PG will have to quarantine and take online classes if available.

These are only a few of the many problems that third year students will face if colleges are compulsorily reopened in an offline mode. I completely understand that on the other hand, this may be a great option for first and second year students and third year students from Delhi NCR. However as a third year student I believe this does more harm than good.

An alternative solution would be to open colleges in the hybrid model (both offline and online). Students from Delhi-NCR can have offline classes and outstation students continue to have online classes as is happening today. This will help contain the number of students, the spread of the virus and help students stay safe. Classes can go on as usual, with the teachers recording the lectures they conduct in class and having consistent doubt clearing sessions. I promise to stay up to date with classes and stay in touch with the professors.

I believe you will reconsider this decision and allow a hybrid model so that outstation students don't face avoidable issues and continue to study as today.

Thank you very much for reading and I genuinely hope you understand my concerns. Hoping for a positive response for you.

Yours respectfully, 
(y/n)
roll no.
course name



mail id: vc@du.ac.in

10/02/2022, 11:04 - mehak kataria: Respected sir/madam

Hope this email finds you well.

We are writing this mail on behalf of the students who are totally unrepresented by political student organisations, and have reservations regarding the re-opening of colleges all of a sudden.

We do have justified reasons for demanding continuation of current online mode of teaching/assessment for the current semester.

Our major reasons being:

1) With due respect to the committee set-up to frame the mode of re-opening of the campuses, it must be acknowledged that the re-opening movement was neither honest, nor transparent, nor representative of all the students of the university, in addition, considering the fact that it was largely driven by politically affiliated student organisations.

2) As rumours of re-opening were making rounds in late 2020, a large number of students had shifted to Delhi, rented apartments and made big changes to their lives, only to redo everything in a few months with the coming of the second/Delta wave. Many students had to face the wrath of landlords' greed as their security amounts were not repaid and police took no action. As your eminence must be aware, there's no reason to assume that the next wave, possibly the deadliest one, will not arrive in the country in the coming months, or even weeks. Since the rate of transmission of the next wave will be even higher than that of the Omicron wave, as your eminence must be aware, the condition of outsider students in Delhi may become disastrous.  

3) On online mode it takes almost one and a half month for colleges to send readings to students in various states of the country. We have just received our books, and it is difficult for average students at this point to shift to another city and spend one month or so in the same, to the point where we are almost reaching exams.

4) Students and their families are not mentally and economically prepared for physical shift to Delhi. Students can consider the situation in which colleges go offline after summer internship period, such that students have time to choose PG/apartments and shift to Delhi, against the sudden reopening. The present situation is having serious psychological impact on a number of unrepresented students, and their capacity to focus on studies has been highly compromised. Shifting will take time and a lot of expenses. At this moment of time, the families are not ready to manage the change in such a short span of time.

5) Many students are engaged in activities like coaching for competitive exams as the online mode of study was expected to continue this semester. Now, it is also not possible to get the fees paid to coaching centres back.

With utmost respect we request the administration to consider our plight, and  the continuation/option of online mode, at least for the current semester.

Thanking you in anticipation.

16/02/2022, 15:59 - Simran Arora: Legal Update:

The matter was heard today at Delhi High Court. Sr Advocate Sanjay Hegde sir represented the students. 

The Court was not inclined to entertain the petition but our issues were pressed by the Sr Adv Sanjay Hegde sir.

The Court was also disinclined to allow online exams.

The Counsel for DU raised objections on maintainability, locus, nature of Writ, PIL jurisdiction and others.

The Court noted that only around 20-24 working days are remaining in the semester, and asked the Counsel for DU if the classes can be conducted in Hybrid mode for the remainder of the semester.

The Counsel for DU has been given time to seek instructions (talk to DU) and file an affidavit.

The order of the notified offline exams scheduled has not been further assailed as the Court was not inclined to interfere with examination order.

The next hearing is scheduled on 22 Feb, 2022 (Tuesday) on the issues of classes.

22/02/2022, 15:35 - Simran Arora: Legal Update:
The matter was heard today. Senior Advocate Sanjay Hegde sir argued for students. The Counsel for DU says 2 months of academic session remains and DDMA says physical mode. He expressed inability to conduct hybrid classes. 
In contrast, Sr Adv. Sanjay Hedge sir argued that even DDMA says meeting should be on VC. Also, what a teacher can do from home can be done from class. He also mentioned that Hostels havenâ€™t even started opening.
The Court asked if DU can give attendance relaxation- let students study themselves 
The network of court collapsed multiple times and thus the matter had to be adjourned. Next hearing will likely be on 24 Feb 2022.

24/02/2022, 10:54 - mehak kataria: The two primary drawbacks of the Apriori Algorithm are:Â 

At each step, candidate sets have to be built.

To build the candidate sets, the algorithm has to repeatedly scan the database.

These two properties inevitably make the algorithm slower. To overcome these redundant steps, a new association-rule mining algorithm was developed named Frequent Pattern Growth Algorithm. It overcomes the disadvantages of the Apriori algorithm by storing all the transactions in a Trie Data Structure.Â

The Court directed that out-station students be given attendance relaxation from 17 Feb 22 to 20 Mar 22.

The Court agreed, and directed, that the attendance relaxation will be available to all the out-station students from 17 Feb to 20 Mar.

13/03/2022, 12:37 - mehak kataria: Aaghaaz recently collaborated with the Delhi Police to celebrate International Women's Day with great enthusiasm. The event happened in stages starting from visiting the Parliament Street Police Station, The DCP's Office and meeting the entire Women Police Force there;  followed by the actual place of event The Princess Park, CP where the SHO of Tilak Marg and the Consultant of Delhi Police joined us. In the end there was a small Nukkad Natak performance by Asmita Theater. The entire event gave everyone a message about the significance of women in our society, how our small steps can empower them and how important is gender equality in society. This event couldn't be possible without the efforts and dedicated of our team who worked hard day and night to make it a success.

13/03/2022, 12:45 - Nistha: Guidelines for ML & DM assignment: 
1. Only one assignment is to be submitted for both the subjects

2. The assignment should be made in softcopy , with the first page containing name of your topic , name of the students submitting the assignment, along with respective roll numbers.

3. Atleast 10 questions are expected (in one assignment , 5/ student) 
4. The assignment is to be done by the pair made in the following images. 

5. Those who haven't received any topic yet are supposed to come to class to get a topic from geetika ma'am.

6. The names in bracket in the given images have to cross check the respective assignments , before submission. 

7. You must include some theory about the algorithm before starting with the questions. Also , please write full questions and use different colours in MS Word to make assignment presentable. 

8. You cannot make a group of 3 people for the assignment. 

9. Please complete this utmost care since this carries 20 marks. 

10. If any of the students have any queries regarding their assignments ,  you can reach out to me (Nishtha) or text geetika ma'am over teams app. Please do not text her over whatsapp.

11. People marked with star have already completed the assignment. 

*Deadline* : 
For first two groups : Mid sem break 

For other groups: End of March i.e. 31st March.

05/04/2022, 10:47 - +91 95205 76470: Thus, methodology of LogR:

To find the values of coefficents B0, B1, B2,â€¦Bk to plug into the equation: y= log(p/(1-p))= Î²0 + Î²1*x1 + â€¦ + Î²k*xk = Bt.X , for specific values of x.

The result of substituting the values of B0,B1,B2,..Bk and the values of x into this equation, is the log-odds of an event (ie log-odds of y=1, given those values of x). Thus, the coefficients are obtained in the log scale.

Now, convert the coefficients into the odds scale and later into probability. Using the value of log-odds (Bt.X) of the event, odds is obtained by e^ (Bt.X). Then, the probability of the event is derived by {e^ (Bt.X)/[1+e^ (Bt.X)] }.

21/04/2022, 10:58 - Nistha: Occam's razor suggests that in machine learning, we should prefer simpler models with fewer coefficients over complex models like ensembles. Taken at face value, the razor is a heuristic that suggests more complex hypotheses make more assumptions that, in turn, will make them too narrow and not generalize well.
